This new system with a power blade works very well. The handle is balanced and easy to grip, and you need to get used to holding it a bit differently because of the system vibration. Very nice, close, painless shave.</li>
    <li> I received the Fusion ProGlide Power razor and handle for free through a Gillette program. The handle is comfortable and sturdy. The rubber enhancements work well. The handle is balanced and easy to grip, and you need to get used to holding it a bit differently because of the vibration. Very well designed!</li>
    <li> I tried the new Gillette Fusion ProGlide razor recently because I got it free through a promotion from Gillette.  I found it to be a great product and provide a very smooth shave.  The handle was very comfortable and easy to maneuver and it really gives a great shave.  The only downside would be that it&#x27;s an expensive proposition on a regular-purchase basis.  That, of course, doesn&#x27;t take anything away from the quality of the product...just a matter of priorities when shopping!  Thanks Gillette...</li>
    <li> I got this razor through a program run by gillette, it is a great handle, comfortable and nimble enough to shave at any angle.  It is also weighted just right so that it provides a comfortable, close shave.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve used the Schick Hydro and MAC3 razors in the past.  I noticed that Gillette was running a program for a free razor and I wanted to test it out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The biggest plus I saw with the Proglide was that the handle was battery operated.  Therefore, it should work very similar to a electric razor.  There is a push button on the front of the handle that allows for the razor to work electrically.  In addition, you just need to turn the bottom of the handle to open the part where the battery is stored.  A very simple process if you need to change it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The handle was very enjoyable to hold.  As most razors are, this handle was made rubber.  I found the grip to be very good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I really enjoyed the design of this handle, however I still felt some tug on the overall shave on my face.  The thicker haired area of my face saw the all the tug (5-6 times around my chin).  However, other areas that were not as thick felt a very smooth and close shave.  In addition, clean up only took a few seconds.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would highly recommend this to the individual with limitied to medium thickness of facial hair.  I rated this 4/5 because it might not be the best option if you have very thick facial hair.</li>
    <li> I am used to the Mach3 Turbo, with its relatively thin handle.  I shave in the shower and found the handle to be a little difficult to handle.  Between the vibration and the soap, it sometimes felt as though I was going to drop the razor.  I will continue using it and see if it is just a matter of getting used to it.</li>
    <li> When I first saw the Fusion ProGlide Power handle, I have to admit I thought it was just a marketing gimmick that would be used to up prices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But I was suprised, it complements the Proglide blades and provides for a much smoother shave and experience than I&#x27;m used to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I received the handle/razor free as part of a program run by Gillette.</li>
    <li> I recently received a free sample of this razor from a Gillete promotion. Usually with these disposable razors the weight and feel of the handle itself is a bit on the light side. Most of the time this is because it is a hollow plastic, as a result I always need to grip tighter to get the right sort of control and pressure I want on the blade. With this razor however, there are two differentiating factors that negate this issue. The first is the riveted handle itself. The grooves within it allow for a more natural and less forced grip on the razor. The second is that because this is a battery operated razor, and that battery is housed in the handle, you get that extra weight that is sorely missing from other disposables. The difference is clear and can be compared to holding a full tang chef&#x27;s knife against holding a wood handled discount knife. The weight and grip, give control of the razor at a more nuanced degree than any other disposable I have tried.</li>
    <li> I love the micropulses handle with the side grips! Even when I get it wet it stays firmly in my hand! Best razor ever and thank you Gillette for giving it free! Now I will be a loyal customer</li>
    <li> Gillette has excellent products and I&#x27;m glad I got in on their promotion to try the razor and blades for free.  I&#x27;m a fan of the blades and handle to a point.  I like the close shave, control and feel of the handle.  I don&#x27;t care for the power feature as I felt I&#x27;d likely cut my chin using it there.  I&#x27;ll continue to use only without the battery.  The non power version is on my list to try next.</li>
    <li> It is great for sensitive skin, no cuts or irritations. It is modern and easy to use, nice handle, great blades. It looks and feels great when using it, better than previous Gillette products. I am glad I was able to try it for free from Gillette.</li>
    <li> Awesome product. I was more than happy to accept this razor from the program by Gillette. The battery last forever and the bottom line is that the razor provides a great shave for a low cost. Before this razor I was using disposables and was going through them after 2-3 shaves. I feel like I get a better shave with this razor without no nicks. Great product.</li>
    <li> My Mach 3 Turbo Power shave handle is getting a little long in the tooth.  I&#x27;ve probably used it for well over 5 years but it has always done a good job, felt solid in my hand and worked exactly like you&#x27;d hope a razor handle to.  When I got the chance to try out the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power handle as part of a free program from Gillette, I was pretty happy to try it out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I got the razor handle, I took it out of the package and got a feel for it.  I even sat and compared it to my Mach 3 Turbo Power handle (which, even at 5 years old, still looks exactly the same as the new Mach 3 Power handles, so I think the comparisons can hold up).  The Fusion ProGlide Power handle was bigger in size and circumference, a tad lighter and had more tacky rubber to the handle than the Mach 3 Power handle.  I can&#x27;t say one is better than the other, but they are both nice and solid and they feel good in the hand.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I think the Fusion ProGlide Power handle looks quite a bit better than the Mach 3, but I don&#x27;t think the cosmetics of either product have a positive or negative impact on their functions.  The Fusion ProGlide Power handle kind of reminds me of Terminator and Robocop all rolled into one and thus, I feel like one bad dude when I use it.  Further speaking to the cosmetic appeal of the Fusion ProGlide Power handle, the power button actually lights up a cool blue which is nothing more than pretty, but I like pretty.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Before using, I placed both razors on a flat surface and turned their power on, which is a slight vibration that is supposed to aid in removing hair for the areas you shave.  Both had fresh batteries for comparison&#x27;s sake.  The Fusion ProGlide Power handle jumped around the table like it was auditioning for So You Think You Can Dance.  The Mach 3 blade moved around, but not quite as much.  That could be a result of years of use or the Fusion Power has that much more vibe, it&#x27;s hard to tell.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once I got to use the Fusion ProGlide Power handle to shave, I liked it quite a bit.  It continued to feel nice in the hand as I shaved my face and head.  One thing that was slightly odd to me was that it felt a bit slippery when it got a lot of water on it.  I wasn&#x27;t expecting that due to all the rubber on the handle, but it was more slippery than my other razor handle.  By no means a deal breaker, it wasn&#x27;t flying out of my hand or anything.  It was just a bit slicker than I expected with water on the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;By the time I was done shaving, I was pretty happy with the handle overall.  It works exactly like you&#x27;d want it to, feels nice in the hand and just for a cherry on top, it looks kinda cool, too.  I&#x27;d gladly recommend the handle to anyone in the market as long as they wanted to go with the 5 blade option.</li>
    <li> Loved the razor!  It gave a comfortable shave that was effortless.  Worth the money, but it is expensive!  I would totally recommend it to anyone.  A really good razor is hard to find and I think I may have found my favorite</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ll admit up front that I didn&#x27;t have to pay for this razor. I got it via a program from Gillette. But after using now for a few days, I&#x27;m definitely planning on buying a second one for my travel kit. This thing is loaded with great features to have a great shave with, but after getting used to the features at the top of the razor, I&#x27;ve been noticing the past couple shaves how nice the handle is. I&#x27;m guessing Gillette did some &#x27;beta testing&#x27; or focus groups or something, because the handle is great. It&#x27;s a bit bigger than what I had before, more suited to a man&#x27;s hand, and the contour is great. Very comfortable to hold. And, when the power is engaged, you really feel connected to the razor handle. Really nice.</li>
    <li> I tried out this razor free as part of a The Gillette Fusion Proglide Power Razor has a nice, solid weight to it, plus bigger, more ergonomic side grips compared to previous versions.  I shave in the shower, so having a a razor I can keep a steady grip on even when it&#x27;s wet is important to me.  The thinner blades of the cartridge make for less tug and pull than some other razors; I&#x27;m sure the good grips, the swiveling head, and the concomitant enhanced maneuverability likewise contribute to the ease of shaving.  I switched to power razors years and years ago--don&#x27;t know whether the vibration actually helps, but I like the feel!  The razor has an automatic turn-off feature as well.</li>
    <li> I am so happy that Gillette came up with the first electric slim handle on a razor! All the electric razors I have had in the past have a very thick handle which makes it harder to get in certain areas of my face, this now allows me to do better triming as well. I would recomend this razor to anyone who uses an electrical razor on a regular basis. Now that I have switched I will not go back to any other electric razor! Thank you gillette for the oportunity to try this razor first!</li>
    <li> I was provided a free Gillette Fusion ProGlide Razor via a program run by Gillette. The handle seemed to be over designed. I didn&#x27;t really notice the improved grip, although I guess that is a good thing since I didn&#x27;t have any problems holding it, even when wet. The large bulb at the bottom was kind of annoying to me and effects the overall aesthetics of the look of the handle, which overall is pretty cool. For many shoppers who make purchases such as these based off the look in the package, such as myself, you might be losing some customers with this bump at the bottom. As for the overall shave, it&#x27;s great. The powered handle seemed to increase the quality of shave and for someone who doesn&#x27;t shave very often, experiences like these make me want to shave more.</li>
    <li> Gillette has made a quality handle that makes shaving easy.  I like the grippiness of the Handle.  The micro pulses from the Duracell battery power make for an effortless close comfortable shave.</li>
    <li> I received the Fusion Power Proglide from Gillette for free as part of a program they are sponsoring to promote the product, the price was right so even though I am primarily an electric user I gave it a try. It is no doubt a quality product &amp; gives a close shave, but I would not attribute any of that to the vibrating handle. It feels good in your hand but did nothing to enhance my shaving experience. Perhaps if I was a regular blade user it may have had more of an impression on me, but the vibrating thing just struck me as gimmicky.</li>
    <li> Love this product for my everyday shave.  It got close and lasted long without irritation. I received it free through a promotion and use it everyday. It comes with a nice holder to keep it save from kids and even has a reflective mirror for quick shaves.  The battery operated vibrations keep it smooth and comfortable.  HIGHLY RECOMMEND</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power handle for a few weeks now (I received them as a free demo through Gillette), and I&#x27;ve got mixed feelings about it. While I like the fact that it&#x27;s thinner and more easily-handled than most of the other powered handles I&#x27;ve used before, I guess I just really don&#x27;t like the vibration aspect. It seems to take the \\&quot;feel\\&quot; out of the shave - makes my fingers numb. I&#x27;ve got a beard/mustache, and do some precision shaving, and the vibration seems to dull the feel I use to get an accurate line.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It does work just fine without being turned on, and is a good enough handle in that case. I prefer a bit more of an angle between the blades and the handle, but this straighter line seems to be where most newer handles are going. The vibrating head is also a cool addition, but I&#x27;m not convinced that it adds to my shave.  It feels pretty much the same to me when I use the vibrating and when I use don&#x27;t use it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The one thing I am stuck on with this handle is that it reminds me of a teenager and his car.  This handle is that 16 year old with a tricked out shiny Honda Civic with loud exhaust and a cool sound system.  Oh, and don&#x27;t forget the sweet rims.  But the problem is just that-- it looks cool, but doesn&#x27;t do anything a normal Civic would not.  This razor looks and feels awesome, but at the end of the day it still shaves my face just like any other razor would.  I have the used normal non-vibrating Gillette for some time now, and I don&#x27;t think this fancier looking, vibrating device makes any difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All things considered, this is really just an average handle that looks cool.  It definitely seems like more a novelty than anything, and some people like that.  Objectively, however, I think that the \\&quot;close shave\\&quot; this handle helps provide is more mind over matter.  Realistically, I get just as close of a shave without vibration and anyone who says otherwise may just be fooled by the cool looks and neat vibration.  Don&#x27;t get me wrong, this handle functions 100% and will give you a good shave, but it&#x27;s not because of the ergonomic grip and electronics.</li>

    <li> I used Gillette cartridge shavers for years; Sensor Excel, Mach 3, the 4-blade system (forgot the name), and Fusion Power. Probably spent thousands of dollars on these contraptions, and for what??--as I&#x27;ve learned, the shave you get from the cartridge razors is simply not as good as old-fashioned straight razor and safety razor shaves. If you don&#x27;t take yourself seriously as a man and as a connoisseur, than by all means, stick with cartridge razors and waste money to boot. But if you value the lofty experience, the pinnacle of manly class and style, try out traditional shaving.&lt;br /&gt;I switched to a safety razor rather than move up to the Proglide. I&#x27;m glad I did.&lt;br /&gt;The best shave you can get, of course, is from a professional barber with a profesionally-maintained straight razor. But that&#x27;s an occasional treat, unless you have the time to go to your barbershop every morning and afternoon for shaves (I hope that tradition makes a comeback, though). Maintaining a straight razor at home is time-consuming. And you have to treat shaving with more care and caution, lest you bloody your shower as in a scary horror flick. The good medium compromise is the famous safety razor, which is making a comeback these days. You buy a safety razor handle, made of heavy metal, usually stainless steel. It feels good, heavy, solid in your hand. You buy an inexpensive supply of safety razor blades. Easy to replace, they last about 1-2 weeks per double-sided blade, dependng on beard thickness. Standard safety blades will do you fine, and they&#x27;re much, much less expensive than constantly buying cartridges which clog and wear out quickly (if you want the best safety razor blades, [...] ([...]) has cryo-treated safety blades that last five times as long as regular safety blades, so you save even more money).&lt;br /&gt;Then, you buy several shaving soaps and soap dishes, for variety if you like, which are better for your skin than mass-market aerosol shaving gels. The mass-market stuff is junk. Traditional shaving soaps last months, are good for your skin, and smell wonderful. The women will love you and your close, clean-smelling shave. I keep five different soaps in my shower in separate bowls so i can switch depending on my mood for scents. You can buy a good quality boar bristle shaving brush for $15, or as part of a set, which you use to apply the soaps from inside the dishes.&lt;br /&gt;For instructions and more information on the old art of traditional shaving, you can also check out The Art of Manliness blog ([...]), which is an enjoyable website for the cultivated man&#x27;s lifestyle.&lt;br /&gt;Simply put, safety razors and straight razors give you a much closer shave, with less irritation, with healthier skin from traditional shaving soaps, that smell better, at a much lower price. And btw, a quality aftershave treatment will also be very good for your skin, it does make a difference. Due to the greater time-consumption of maintaining a straight razor, I suggest trying a safety razor outfit first.shaving soaps last months, are good for your skin, and smell wonderful. Surely there are more of you who have noticed this disturbing trend of late?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am of Italian heritage with a heavy beard - I shave more whiskers in one stroke than most peach-fuzz Caucasians shave in a whole week...&lt;br /&gt;So if I don&#x27;t need all these blades &amp; tacky gimmicks - then no one does.&lt;br /&gt;All anyone requires is the original twin blade Sensor - loud, proud &amp; simple. But they are way too wide to get at any tight spots like under your nose, upper lip, or any side-burn/mustache trimming. Gillette&#x27;s solution is to flip over to a single trimming blade on the back. But here is where this entire concept fails: now we are down to the use &amp; life of just this one blade!&lt;br /&gt;Get it?&lt;br /&gt;Once this one \\&quot;trimming\\&quot; blade is dull, the whole $3.00+ blade goes in the garbage!&lt;br /&gt;So really - it does not last any longer than a twin blade! With the old Sensor, we had the advantage of two blades hitting all the tight spots.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And then there is this useless &amp; goofy \\&quot;power\\&quot; business. So now, not only are we being forced to fork over $3.00+ per blade...but now we also have to start buying batteries. Gillette&#x27;s stance on the environment? Well evidently their position is to now have millions more batteries going into our landfills. Lovely.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And yes, Gillette is clearly bullying the marketplace as we longtime loyal customers can no longer find our favorites in the stores. And if we do - they are now priced double of what they were just a few short years ago. In fact, last time I found my Sensors at Walmart - there was a big sticker on the box asking the customer to call a 1-800 number to inform them if we \\&quot;see this product being sold elsewhere\\&quot;!! So much for competition and the free market economy!&lt;br /&gt;I remember everyone used to just go into the shaving aisle at the stores, grab their fave blades and leave. Now these aisles are full of price-shocked guys standing around scratching their heads, wondering what to do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OK, I understand that Gillette cannot effectively inventory all the retailers with every generation of product they ever made. I also believe in the evolution and optional availability of an evolved product. But give us the option of buying a simple twin Sensor blade at an affordable price and keep it readily available. But here Gillette has us over the barrel and is literally forcing everyone to pay a premium for what many of us do not believe is any better (in fact - annoyingly worse).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If not, then I would say that this is an opportune time for the competition like Wilkinson Sword to step up and hit this sweet spot by heavily marketing that sorely missed twin blade at an reasonable price. They would clean house. Unfortunately, I myself have not experimented much with the competition because of hit &amp; miss availability. Don&#x27;t want to find something one week - and then get stuck without the next.     <li> When I was younger, I used electric razors, Norelco and Braun types, and thought they were fine; I was a bit intimidated by manual shaving. Then when I got a older I disliked the fact I could never shave very close with those razors, leading to afternoon beard shadows. Plus, it was hard to do anything like trim a smart goatee or sideburns, not to mention the heads would wear out periodically, and were expensive to replace.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally I moved to shaving cream and manual razors, and it was like graduating to the big leagues, or moving from an automatic transmission to a stick-shift. I felt more in control and got a much better shave that lasted all day. But with cheap razors I found I&#x27;d end up with nicks and irritations no matter how carefully I shaved. I&#x27;m the type of shaver who goes against the grain; otherwise, I&#x27;d never get close enough (my beard grows pretty fast).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve tried most of the hyped-up Gillette and Schick razors over the years, and while they were a definite improvement over the throwaway kind, they were never all they were cracked up to be - I just figured razor technology had gone about as far as it could go, and adding more blades or a gimmick like battery power were just oneupmanship between the two major brands to win market share.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That is, until I decided to give this Fusion Proglide Power a shot. I should say right up front, I&#x27;ve not used the non-power version, so I can&#x27;t comment on whether the vibration is a gimmick or does something useful. But I will say I haven&#x27;t had a better shave except from a barber! The basic razor (and especially the starter kit) are not expensive, for what they are. The \\&quot;hidden\\&quot; cost, of course, is the price of the blades (and the Fusion creams if you choose to use their brand). This could be a big drawback for some, but I value the comfortable, nick-free shave this razor gives me and the extra cost is worth it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In my experience, the only better shave you can get is from a straight razor or good safety razor with the old-fashioned shaving soap and brush. But that makes a mess and is hard to master. I was actually going to try that route before I bought the Proglide... now, I don&#x27;t have to! This razor does what it says, and the space between the blades stays remarkable clean as well. I&#x27;m used to having to dip my razor in the water, tap it hard on the back, or some other way to unclog the blades after every few strokes. Not so with this one. Maybe because the blades are thinner? I don&#x27;t know, but it just seems like it never clogs, even with some heavy growth to mow. That&#x27;s another big plus in my book.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I dunno about buying into the whole Gillette \\&quot;system\\&quot; of warm-up washes, Fusion creams, and cooling aftershave. I think those products are overpriced and I can surely find cheaper brands that work just as well. But as to the razor itself (or more precisely, its blades), I have to give this product 5 stars. Do I wish the blades were cheaper? Sure. But I don&#x27;t mind paying for something when it&#x27;s actually worth the extra money, and to me at least, the shave this gives my fairly sensitive skin and course beard definitely makes it worth the money. Good job this time around, Gillette.ith the old-fashioned shaving soap and brush. But that makes a mess and is hard to master. I was exceptionally surprised when after my first shave I had decided that I would go out and purchase a replacement cartridge right away. Yes, it was THAT good. Imagine my surprise when I went to purchase a replacement 4pack cartridge and discovered it was just under $5 cheaper than the regular Fusion 4pack and nearly $7 cheaper than the Proglides. In fact, it was about the exact same price as what I was paying for Mach 3 cartridges some 5 YEARS ago. Cheaper razors that last longer and still give me a top notch razor-burn-free shave adds up to one very converted former Gillette fanboy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To sum it up: did the Proglide shave great? YES. In fact it was a superior shave all around. Would I recommend buying one? Well, that depends. Personally I doubt I&#x27;ll pay for anotherProglide razor ever again. I simply cannot justify the cost vs getting a shave JUST AS GOOD from my Hydro 5 for a great deal cheaper. Reading some other reviews here at amazon I have noticed something interesting, former Schick fans who have converted to Gillette saying the Proglide is better or superior and whatnot...but I found that for ME, the opposite was true. While the Proglide provided a great shave, the Hydro 5 did the same job for much less...and with money tight the way it is these days, I need to cut corners where possible, and the Schick razor allows me to do that without sacrificing a fantastic shave in the process. Either way, if you have the money, buy what works for YOU and don&#x27;t let anybody tell you different.not justify the cost vs getting a shave JUST AS GOOD from my Hydro 5 for a great deal cheaper.     <li> To properly evaluate the new Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power razor, I decided to compare it to the new Schick Hydro 5 and my normal razor, a Schick Quattro Power. All started with a new cartridge and a fresh battery as applicable.    I&#x27;ll begin by saying that I&#x27;ve been using Schick razors for about 40 years and have not been too impressed by most Gillette razors. In particular, they tended to clog up more and were harder to keep clean. I was expecting to be underwhelmed by the ProGlide as well.    ProGlide vs. Hydro 5  Initial impressions:  Packaging: Both come in the standard plastic clamshell, but the Gillette is easier to open. The back is perforated for easy opening, where the Schick is more child-proof and requires a sharp object to open it.    What&#x27;s included: The Gillette comes with only one cartridge, where the Hydro comes with two.    Holders: the Gillette snaps snugly in to the included plastic holder, while the Schick holder just has a small pin to locate the razor. You could use the Gillette&#x27;s as a travel holder with no problem.    Guarantee: The Schick comes with a money back guarantee. The Gillette assumes you will like it.    The razors: While the Gillette looks more substantial, both weigh 1.4 oz fully loaded.  The Gillette has a single blade trimmer on the back  of the cartridge. Flip the razor 180 deg to use it. The Hydro&#x27;s trimmer is under the lube strip that you flip back to use the trimmer.    Cartridge mounting: The ProGlide cartridge slides on easily and snaps in place. The locator pin also acts as \\&quot;suspension\\&quot; for the cartridge pivot. The Hydro is a bit more imprecise. You have to line up two small spring loaded fingers on the handle with tabs on the cartridge. Not hard, but not as elegant as the Gillette. The Schick cartridge is smaller than the Gillette...less waste.    On initial \\&quot;hefting\\&quot; the Gillette felt better, but in use both were comfortable and easy to maneuver.    The Shave Test  All of the above are secondary to the \\&quot;Yes, But How Does It Shave\\&quot; test. I shaved half of my face with the Gillette and half with the Schick, using [[ASIN:B000RI8BZQ Proraso Shaving Cream]] and a badger bristle brush.    Shave No. 1: (3 Day Growth)  The ProGlide felt smooth in all directions, with and against the grain. No pulling on the neck or under the chin. The trimmer was easy to use.    The Hydro was smooth on the cheeks, but pulled noticeably on the neck, especially against the grain. It left a couple of small \\&quot;razor burn\\&quot; marks on my neck. To use the trimmer you have to hold the razor with one hand and flip back the cover with the other.    Both razors rinsed clean easily with no clogging.    The Wife Test: Immediately after shaving, Mrs. Boilermate judged the Gillette side marginally smoother, but said that side felt sticky. After my face \\&quot;dried\\&quot; she still said the Gillette side was smoother.    Shave No. 2: (2 Day Growth)  The Gillette was smooth while the Hydro pulled noticeably on the neck and under the chin. The Gillette side was again judged smoother in the Wife Test.    ProGlide vs Quattro  Shave Nos. 3 and 4 were done with a two and three day growth respectively using the ProGlide and a Schick Power Quattro (with a new cartridge and a fresh battery).    The first thing I noticed is the ProGlide is noticeably quieter, where the Quattro sounds like an electric razor by comparison.    In both tests, the ProGlide performed as before, with no pulling or burning. The Quattro pulled slightly on the neck, but substantially less than the Hydro did.    As before, the Gillette side was judged smoother by Mrs. B., tho by a similarly small margin.    So what&#x27;s not to like? The price of the cartridges. Schick cartridges are cheaper across the board than Gillette. Power ProGlide carts are about $4.00 apiece, where Quattro Power carts are about $2.50 each.    While the ProGlide gives an excellent shave, doesn&#x27;t shave enough better to justify switching from the Quattro based on the cost of the cartridges.    Overall, though, the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power rates five stars. As a life-long Schick user, I was pleasantly (and unexpectantly) surprised by this razor. If you can get past the price of the cartridges, I highly recommend this razor.</li>
    <li> I just got a sample of this razor from Gillette and I have to say its not much more different than the older Fusion.     <li> I tried every razor on the market starting with the Gillette sensor 2 blade when I first started shaving at around 14-15 years of age. The truth is that I kept on buying into the newer razors that came out thinking they were better but that was always not the case. So I&#x27;ll briefly compare this to the other razors I&#x27;ve tried and tell you a honest view of mine about why this deserves only one star and which razors are better.    Firstly, when I started shaving the Gillette sensor excel 2 blade was excellent and provided a good shave with less to no irritation at all when used with a shave gel. The sensor 3 blade was a little closer and just as comfortable as the two blade. Thats all I have to say about that.  The Mach 3 then came out which did seem to be a better razor and provided a closer shave with out much irritation so it was a winner. Then Mach 3 power nitro came out and the power aspect felt good but the results was basically the same. So all in all the Mach 3 manual and power were better than the Sensor excel 2 and 3 blade razors up to now.    Schick then came out with the quattro 4 blade(the original first one) which was Ok and provided a good close shave but I still decided to stick with the comfort of the Mach 3. So up till now the Mach 3 was my razor of choice.    Now the story changes a bit:    I received a free sample of the fusion power and at first I thought it was the best razor because of the first few close shaves it provided. I got over excited and bought a 8 pack refill for the fusion power thinking I would never use anything else. BAD DECISION!!!! My clear unirritated skin became red and irritated after continuing to use the fusion power. At first I thought maybe my skin is changing as I&#x27;m getter older so it&#x27;s my skin&#x27;s fault. I would get ingrown hairs and it was then embarrassing to go out. I lost all my self confidence and started staying more reserved. I tried various skin treatments to rid of the irritations and redness but nothing would work. The problem with the fusion was that the blades would only last about 3 shaves and then irritate the hell out of your face. ONE DAY I DECIDED IT WAS TIME TO TRY ANOTHER RAZOR.    I then bought the Schick Quattro Titanium and boy was it a much less irritating shave with more comfort and the same closeness as the fusion. It was much much better than the fusion because of the titanium coating and the blades last forever. They would stay sharp for months and wouldn&#x27;t clog if a shave gel was used.(I know people complain that it clogs but with a light foaming shave gel like Anthony Logistics or Zirh it doesn&#x27;t).    Now Hydro 5 vs. Fusion Proglide    Hydro 5 came out first and since the schick quattro titanium was my razor of choice I had to try the Hydro 5. At first I liked it, the gel strip felt gooey but washed off easy with warm water. The shave was not as close as I would have wanted. The hydro 5 missed a few parts on the neck area and the under nose area because of the huge cartridge. Still I kept on using it since it came with 2 refills anyway. The gel strip lasted longer than fusion but not as long as quattro titanium.    Fusion Proglide: I bought the sneak peek package just to try the razor before it came out and all I can say is AWFULLLLLL!!!!!!! This time I couldn&#x27;t even get one good shave from this crap. Turns shaving into gliding my A$$!!!! It&#x27;s very uncomfortable to use and does not glide at all.I will admit that it provides a very close shave but that irriates my face a lot. So the fusion proglide is the worst razor I&#x27;ve ever used so far. The cartridge lasts only like two shaves and the refills are more expensive than a full tank of gasoline(mind the exaggeration but you know what I mean).    Final verdict: Gillette just tweaks their razors a bit makes false claims and sells their refills for a lot of money to fool the consumers. They are nothing but marketing now. Up until the Mach 3 they were my razor brand but the fusion and fusion proglide are nothingbut scams. They look cool but I think they are face wreckers. Then again I have sensitive skin so I understand people with thicker beards and normal skin probably love Gillette razors but I have to address the sensitive skin shavers out there and Gillette razors should be avoided by them unless they want a irritated face.    The hydro 5 lost because of the huge razor head and strip making it less precise. Also the skin guards on the hydro irritate more than help. So Schick Quattro Titanium is the razor of choice for my sensitive skin. It will not clog with Zirh or Anthony Logistics shave gel and causes no irritation. The blade lasts long and refills are reasonable price, it has the single edging blade which is better than hydro 5 flip trimmer which just irritates. Sorry for long review but I just had to share my experience.</li>

    <li> Some of us may recall that the &amp;#34;tool&amp;#34; our fathers used to shave with was called a straight razor. (Another use was when an older brother had his rear tanned when he got out of line!)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To use a straight razor,  the angle where the  razor met the skin for shaving was very important.  An incorrect angle and the skin would be cut.  The other item of importance was the amount of  pressure applied to the razor during the shaving.  Too much force and a cut usually resulted. Too little force and hair  was not shaved off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The safety razor came into  being when a guy named Gillette devised a &amp;#34;tool&amp;#34; to eliminate the need  to hold the razor at a precise angle to shave the face.     <li> Let me start out by saying that if you&#x27;re absolutely settled on a cartridge razor system, this or the regular Fusion Proglide will probably fit the bill just fine. As far as multi-blade razors go, this is the most comfortable shave I&#x27;ve experienced from one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With that said, here&#x27;s the deal. For the longest time I simply used regular old Gillette Mach 3 disposables and bought some more every time I ran out. They never gave me a great shave, but I chocked that up to my sensitive skin and thought razor burn and bumps were unavoidable. I figured at the very most I&#x27;d need to simply find a better shaving foam/gel, but I never did find it. Finally, I decided to &#x27;upgrade&#x27;, and bought one of these at CVS for $10.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Fusion Proglide does offer superior performance over standard disposables, of course. In terms of cartridge razor &#x27;systems&#x27;, this is as good as it gets. I don&#x27;t think that the &#x27;Power&#x27; model is necessary, although it&#x27;s what I got. The vibrating feature can sometimes feel nice, but most of the time I just shave with it normally.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s why I say it turned me off of cartridge systems forever. I went from standard disposables to this, and instead of getting a lot better shave and/or saving money, I got a marginally better shave for quite a bit of money. The razor itself is only about $10, but cartridges are currently $32 for 8 cartridges on Amazon! At the very most - and I think I&#x27;m being a bit too generous here - this is a 2-month supply, assuming each cartridge lasts a week which I highly doubt. That&#x27;s at least $192 a year just on cartridges! (Although, I believe you can use regular Fusion Proglide cartridges, although they aren&#x27;t much cheaper).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, I don&#x27;t mean to sound like a salesman here, but I do have another suggestion. After realizing I couldn&#x27;t justify $200 a year on cartridges, I was absolutely sure there had to be a cheaper way to shave that didn&#x27;t involve an electric razor which doesn&#x27;t get close enough. Amazon \\&quot;Top Rated\\&quot; directed me to an old-school Merkur double-edged safety razor, and I read up. I&#x27;m not trying to sell you guys a Merkur. Buy whatever safety razor floats your boat, but hear this out: 100 razor blades for $10. Razor blades that are sharper and probably last just as long as the cartridges (and perform better), for much, much cheaper. Even if they each only last 3-4 days, that&#x27;s still a years supply for around $10 as opposed to $192. I&#x27;m no math major, but I think that&#x27;s a savings of about $182.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I got tired of paying for a cartridge system that doesn&#x27;t shave as well as an old-school safety razor, irritates my face, and costs literally hundreds of dollars a year. It didn&#x27;t make sense to me. In a week or two of using a DE razor, I&#x27;ve made irritation literally a thing of the past. The thing glides along the face, hardly feeling like it&#x27;s touching you until you realize the hair is gone. Honestly, it&#x27;s an epiphany that I can&#x27;t keep quiet about. Especially if you&#x27;ve got sensitive skin, make the switch and save a lot of money.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;m a Schick Quattro user, and have been for a lot of years, but Gillette sent me a free Fusion ProGlide Power through a promotional program, so I figured I&#x27;d give it a try.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My shaving needs might be a bit different from most guys in that I have a beard, but I shave my head.     <li> I have been using the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power razor for three weeks now and have been pleasantly surprised by the results. To give some background, I have a tough, thick beard that grows back fairly quickly. I work in an industry where it is important to maintain a clean-cut look. I have found that electric razors have not been able to provide a close enough shave for me and have been using the Gillette Mach3 for the past several years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had sampled the Gillette Fusion Power when it first released and was extremely dissatisfied with the experience, so I returned to my Mach3. I found that the lubricated strip wore out after the first use, the micropulses from the battery were weak and ineffective, and water leaked into the battery compartment causing damage to the product. As a result, I had very low expectations from the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I received a sample Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power handle and cartridge through a program sponsored by Gillette. It appears that most of the negative issues that I had encountered on the Gillette Fusion Power have been addressed. I didn&#x27;t expect that there could be any noticeable improvement to my shaves with 5 blade technology, battery powered micropulses, and a lubristrip but I couldn&#x27;t have been more wrong. The Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power razor delivered the smoothest shave I have ever had - not only on the first use but also after repeated uses. I could really feel the battery powered micropulses in conjuction with the microcomb lift the hairs up and guide them in a uniform direction for a closer cut. The lubristrip allowed for smooth strokes and as a result, the razor was gliding effortlessly. The mineral oil from the lubristrips also left my skin feeling soft and irritation-free. The power of 5 blades meant that I did not have to repeat my strokes. With all these efficiencies, there is literally no friction (ie. no tugging and pulling) or discomfort. The razor glides effortlesslyand also provides a very close shave - which is exactly what I have been looking for.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ergonomic design of the handle made it easy to grip but because of the large size of the 5-blade cartridge, I still found the product difficult to maneuver around the tight spots around the sideburns and below the nose. The product advertises a precision trimmer, which is supposed to help with these areas, but I&#x27;m not sure it completely addresses the problem with maneuvering such a large cartridge. I have noticed that I have been becoming more adept with repeated use, so perhaps it is an acquired skill but it is definitely a noticeable different handle in comparison to the Mach3. The handle also has an automatic shutoff feature if the battery power is left on after 8 minutes. I did not use this feature, but think it is a good safeguard in case someone does accidently leave the power on. When I had used the Gillette Fusion Power, I had noticed damage to the battery compartment due to water leakage. Fortunately, they have addressed that issue in this product. When I opened up the handle, there were no traces of water having leaked into the battery compartment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I tested the razor under multiple conditions over the past three weeks: 1 day shave, 3 day shave, and 1 week shave. In each situation, the result was a smooth, close shave. With the 1 day shave, where I had limited hair regrowth, I did experience a few nicks below the nose but because of the mineral oil from the lubristrip, I could not even notice the cuts. Normally on the 3 day shave, I have significant regrowth by the end of the 2nd day but because of the closer shave from the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power, I didn&#x27;t notice the same level of regrowth until the middle of the 3rd day! The product was also able to handle a 1 week shave with the same level of effortlessness. Normally, with my Mach3, the hairs would get stuck inside the blades and I have to make repeat strokes over the same areas, but with the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power, I was able to still complete the shave in single, deep strokes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My only complaint is that the lubristrip has started to wear out and appear white after 4 shaves, which means that I would expect that I would have to replace cartridges after ever 2-3 weeks of regular use (ie. shaving every 3 days). If you continue to use the cartridge after the lubristrip has worn out, you will lose some of the benefits of the product&#x27;s smooth shave. Given the high prices of the replacement cartridges, this could prove to be the factor that deters me from becoming a convert. I would really like the cartridge to last at least month and am disappointed that it has shown signs of wear after only limited use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I rate the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power handle 5 stars, because it really does fulfill what it is advertised to do and offers the closest shave a man can get, primarily because of the battery powered micropulses, flexibility, and ergonomic design. Any difficulties maneuvering around the tight spots can be corrected with practice. The Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power cartridge, however, has its drawback and I would only give it 2 stars because of how quickly the lubristrip wears out. The 5-blades and microcomb allow for a smooth shave and remain resilient after repeated uses, but because the lubristrip wears out, the cartridge needs to be trashed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will probably keep the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power handle and use it with my Mach3 cartridges (they seem to fit) and only use the more expensive Fusion ProGlide cartridges on special occasions when I need a particularly close shave.</li>

    <li> To be clear, I was offered a Fusion ProGlide to test by Gillette. My normal razor is an Edwin Jagger safety razor. Which leads us to my first point: The blades for the Fusion ProGlide are around 4 bucks each. With my safety razor, I can get 10 Feather blades for about the same price. The Fusion boasts 5 blades, and they tout them as being narrower than others, with a coating designed to cause less \\&quot;tug and pull\\&quot;. I would think that any adequately sharpened blade would also prevent \\&quot;tug and pull\\&quot;. The handle takes an AAA battery, which causes the handle to vibrate. It also increases profits for Duracell, Gillettes sister company. If it sounds daunting to place 5 vibrating razor blades onto your face, relax. The vibration isn&#x27;t really noticeable, and I&#x27;m not sure that it&#x27;s even a benefit, judging from the closeness of the shave, and the United States court system, which judged Gillettes claims about the razor to be \\&quot;unsubstantiated and innaccurate\\&quot;. It seems gimmicky to me. I have an extremely coarse beard, and spent years searching for a close, comfortable shave. I ended up with the shaving kit that our grandfathers used. My single blade, double edged safety razor doesn&#x27;t clog, and I normally shave every other day. The 5 blades DID clog with my coarse hair. I have no patience for that. The accompanying literature says that the built-in \\&quot;guide comb\\&quot; directs hairs into the blades, at the \\&quot;optimum angle\\&quot; for cutting. I don&#x27;t know what the optimum angle is, but I have trouble believing that every hair requires the same angle for a smooth cut, given that I have to shave in several directions. Maybe I&#x27;m wrong. There&#x27;s a trimmer on the back that I don&#x27;t use. It gives a close enough shave when new, but the clogging was a deal breaker for me. I&#x27;m spoiled with a single blade that rinses out with ease. The vibrating handle? Meh. Call me a luddite, but I don&#x27;t need gimmicky tech in a razor. I need a comfortable handle and a sharp blade. The Fusion handle IS comfortable and sturdy, but not as sturdy as my brass and chrome standby, I&#x27;d bet. All in all, it&#x27;s a fine razor, but the cost of blades and all of the unnecessary bells and whistles make it seem a bit silly to me. And the shave? My Edwin Jagger still shaves closer.y, but not as sturdy as my brass and chrome standby, I&#x27;d bet. All in all, it&#x27;s a fine razor, but the cost of blades and all of the unnecessary bells and whistles make it seem a bit silly to me. And the shave? My Edwin Jagger still shaves closer.</li>

I even had a barber shave my face in which he stated I had the toughest facial hair he has ever encountered. But the ProGlide definitely makes life so much easier for me. The finer blades help glide across my face without so much tugging. The Microcomb definitely helps against stray stubble. The indicator strip really lets you know when it&#x27;s time to change the blade, which in my case isn&#x27;t very often, thankfully. The handle grip is excellent and flexible. I don&#x27;t find myself with any shaving cream residue residing on it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So with that said I wondered why it needed an upgrade with the new Power feature. This was a curious thing when I saw that a battery was included. The power button is on the handle so you are able to turn it on and off. The vibrating feature helps make your shaving experience much more relaxing. In addition it&#x27;s also supposed to imitate what an electric shaver feels like against your face complete with the humming and noise. Quite honestly it didn&#x27;t add anything to my experience. It&#x27;s a strange thing to have on a straight edge razor like this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power Handle is great as a razor but doesn&#x27;t need the extra vibrating feature to make the shaving experience beneficial.
